# 随机池 — 日常背词

> 这些词不便归类，适合每天随机抽取 30 个和分组词混合背诵。

**1622 词**

---

## China

- **音标**: 'tʃainә
- **释义**: n. 中国, 瓷器\na. 中国的
- **英文释义**: 1. a country in East Asia; 2. hard, white, translucent ceramic material traditionally made in China
- **词根词缀**: 来自梵语Cina，意为中国
- **例句**:
- China has played a pivotal role in shaping global economic governance in recent decades.
- The museum's collection includes Ming dynasty china renowned for its exquisite craftsmanship and delicate glaze.
- **考频**: 162
## Conservative

- **音标**: kәn'sә:vәtiv
- **释义**: a. 保守的, 守旧的, 有保存力的\n[化] 防腐剂; 保存剂
- **英文释义**: tending to resist change and adhere to traditional values, practices, or beliefs; preserving existing conditions or substances
- **词根词缀**: con(加强)+serv(保持)+ative(形容词)→保持的→保守的
- **例句**:
- The government adopted a conservative fiscal policy to avoid inflationary pressures.
- Calcium propionate is used as a conservative in bread to inhibit mold growth.
- **考频**: 55
## Easter

- **音标**: 'i:stә
- **释义**: n. 复活节
- **英文释义**: A Christian festival celebrating the resurrection of Jesus Christ, observed on the first Sunday after the first full moon following the vernal equinox.
- **词根词缀**: aster(star)
- **例句**:
- Easter is traditionally marked by church services, family gatherings, and the exchange of decorated eggs.
- Many universities in the UK close for a two-week break over Easter, allowing students to travel or rest before final exams.
## Latin

- **音标**: 'lætin
- **释义**: n. 拉丁人, 拉丁语\na. 拉丁人的, 拉丁语的
- **英文释义**: A member of a people originally from Latium in ancient Italy, or the Italic language spoken by them and used as the official language of the Roman Empire; also used to refer to modern Romance-language-speaking peoples or their cultural heritage.
- **词根词缀**: lat(carry/bring/side)+in
- **例句**:
- Latin is still used in scientific nomenclature and the Roman Catholic liturgy.
- The study of Latin grammar and classical texts remains an essential part of many humanities curricula in elite universities.
## Marxist

- **音标**: 'mɑ:ksist
- **释义**: a. 马克思主义的\nn. 马克思主义者
- **英文释义**: relating to or adhering to the political and economic theories of Karl Marx; a person who supports or practices Marxism
- **词根词缀**: mar(sea)+x+-ist(…主义者/…家/从事…者)
- **例句**:
- Her dissertation offers a Marxist analysis of class struggle in 19th-century industrial Britain.
- While not all socialists are Marxists, many contemporary leftist movements draw heavily on Marxist theory.
## Polish

- **音标**: 'pɒliʃ
- **释义**: a. 波兰的\nn. 波兰人, 上光剂, 光泽, 优雅\nvt. 擦亮, 擦去, 使完美\nvi. 擦亮, 变得光亮
- **英文释义**: 1. adj. of or relating to Poland or its people, language, or culture; 2. n. the official language of Poland, a Slavic language; 3. n. a substance used to make surfaces shiny; 4. n. refinement or elegance in manner or style; 5. v. to make smooth, glossy, or perfect through careful effort
- **词根词缀**: Polish(词根:波兰)→波兰的
- **例句**:
- The diplomat's speech reflected years of cultural immersion and linguistic polish.
- Before the exhibition, the curator spent hours polishing the antique silver to restore its original luster.
- **考频**: 28
## Saint

- **音标**: seint
- **释义**: n. 圣徒, 圣人\na. 神圣的\n[计] 自动积分程序符号
- **英文释义**: A person officially recognized by the Christian Church as holy and worthy of public veneration; also used figuratively to describe someone exceptionally virtuous or patient.
- **词根词缀**: saint(圣)→圣徒
- **例句**:
- Mother Teresa was canonized as a saint by the Catholic Church in 2016.
- After enduring years of criticism with grace, she was jokingly called a saint by her colleagues.
- **考频**: 4
## abandon

- **音标**: /əˈbændən/
- **词性**: v.
- **释义**: ==抛弃，遗弃；放弃==
- **英文释义**: to leave somebody, especially somebody you are responsible for; to stop doing an activity
- **同义词**: desert, forsake, relinquish, give up
- **反义词**: keep, retain, maintain
- **词根词缀**: a(加强)+band(带子)+on→带子被丢弃→抛弃
- **搭配**: abandon hope, abandon the idea, abandon a plan
- **例句**:
- Those who abandon hope will never achieve their goals.
- The crew abandoned the sinking ship.
- **考频**: 91
## abide

- **音标**: ә'baid
- **词性**: v.
- **释义**: ==vi. 停留, 遵守, 居留, 继续下去\nvt. 忍受, 经受, 屈从于==
- **英文释义**: v dwell\nv put up with something or somebody unpleasant
- **同义词**: endure, tolerate, comply with
- **反义词**: disobey, reject
- **词根词缀**: ab-(away, from)+ide (Old English 'īdan', to remain, dwell)→literally 'to remain away (from transgression)' or 'to stay in place'→vi. to remain, dwell, or comply; vt. to endure (as in 'bearing up under' something)
- **搭配**: abide by a rule/law/agreement, abide the consequences, abide in faith
- **例句**:
- I cannot abide dishonesty in the workplace.
- She abides by the rules without question.
- **考频**: 5
## ability

- **音标**: ә'biliti
- **词性**: n.
- **释义**: ==n. 能力, 才干\n[经] 能力, 才能==
- **英文释义**: n. the quality of being able to perform; a quality that permits or facilitates achievement or accomplishment\nn. possession of the qualities (especially mental qualities) required to do something or get something done
- **同义词**: capacity, competence, capability
- **反义词**: inability, incapacity
- **词根词缀**: abil(able, capable)+-ity(noun-forming suffix indicating state or quality)→state of being able→the quality or power to do something→ability
- **搭配**: ability to do something, lack of ability, develop one's abilities
- **例句**:
- She has an exceptional ability to learn languages quickly.
- The job requires strong analytical abilities and attention to detail.
- **考频**: 514
## abnormal

- **音标**: æb'nɒ:mәl
- **词性**: adj.
- **释义**: ==a. 反常的, 不规则的, 变态的, 畸形的\nn. 畸形的人==
- **英文释义**: a. not normal; not typical or usual or regular or conforming to a norm\na. departing from the normal in e.g. intelligence and development\ns. much greater than the normal
- **同义词**: irregular, unusual
- **反义词**: normal, regular
- **词根词缀**: ab(偏离)+normal(正常的)→反常的
- **搭配**: abnormal growth, abnormal behavior, abnormal development
- **例句**:
- Her blood pressure readings were consistently abnormal, prompting further medical investigation.
- The software displayed abnormal behavior after the latest update, crashing repeatedly without error messages.
- **考频**: 15
## abolish

- **音标**: ә'bɒliʃ
- **词性**: v.
- **释义**: ==vt. 废止, 革除, 消灭\n[经] 废除, 取消, 裁撤==
- **英文释义**: v. do away with
- **同义词**: eliminate, cancel, eradicate
- **反义词**: establish, maintain
- **词根词缀**: ab(去掉)+olish(生长)→废除
- **搭配**: abolish slavery, abolish a law, abolish discrimination
- **例句**:
- The government decided to abolish the outdated tax law.
- Many countries have abolished the death penalty in recent decades.
- **考频**: 26
## abrupt

- **音标**: ә'brʌpt
- **词性**: adj.
- **释义**: ==a. 突然的, 唐突的, 陡峭的, 不连贯的==
- **英文释义**: s. marked by sudden changes in subject and sharp transitions\ns. exceedingly sudden and unexpected\ns. extremely steep\ns. surprisingly and unceremoniously brusque in manner
- **同义词**: sudden, unexpected
- **反义词**: gradual, expected
- **词根词缀**: ab(离开)+rupt(断裂)→突然断裂→突然的
- **搭配**: abrupt change, abrupt stop, abrupt departure
- **例句**:
- The meeting ended in an abrupt silence when the CEO walked in.
- The road makes an abrupt turn just before the cliff edge.
- **考频**: 8
## absence

- **音标**: 'æbsәns
- **释义**: ==n. 缺席, 缺乏, 没有\n[医] 失神==
- **英文释义**: n. the state of being absent\nn. failure to be present\nn. the time interval during which something or somebody is away\nn. the occurrence of an abrupt, transient loss or impairment of consciousness (which is not subsequently remembered), sometimes with light twitching, fluttering eyelids, etc.; common in petit mal epilepsy
- **同义词**: lack, nonexistence
- **反义词**: presence, attendance
- **词根词缀**: ab(离开)+sence(存在)→不存在→缺席
- **搭配**: absence from, in the absence of
- **例句**:
- His absence from school was noticed.
- In the absence of evidence, we cannot proceed.
- **考频**: 62
## absolute

- **音标**: 'æbsәlu:t
- **释义**: ==a. 绝对的, 专制的, 完全的, 独立的\nn. 绝对事物==
- **英文释义**: n. something that is conceived or that exists independently and not in relation to other things; something that does not depend on anything else and is beyond human control; something that is not relative\na. perfect or complete or pure\ns. complete and without restriction or qualification; sometimes used informally as intensifiers\ns. not limited by law
- **同义词**: complete, total
- **反义词**: relative, partial
- **词根词缀**: ab(脱离)+solute(松开)→脱离限制的→绝对的
- **搭配**: absolute zero, absolute power, absolute truth
- **例句**:
- I have absolute confidence in you.
- The absolute truth is hard to find.
- **考频**: 28
## absorb

- **音标**: /əbˈzɔːrb/
- **词性**: v.
- **释义**: ==吸收；吸引…的注意；使全神贯注==
- **英文释义**: to take in a liquid, gas or heat; to keep somebody's attention
- **同义词**: assimilate, engage, occupy
- **反义词**: release, emit, repel
- **词根词缀**: ab(加强)+sorb(吸收)→强烈吸收
- **搭配**: be absorbed in, absorb attention, absorb information
- **例句**:
- The book absorbs readers with its vivid descriptions.
- Plants absorb carbon dioxide from the atmosphere.
- **考频**: 77
## abstract

- **音标**: /ˈæbstrækt/
- **词性**: adj./n.
- **释义**: ==抽象的；摘要，概论==
- **英文释义**: existing as an idea rather than as something physical; a summary
- **同义词**: theoretical, conceptual, summary
- **反义词**: concrete, specific, practical
- **词根词缀**: abs(离开)+tract(拉)→拉开→抽象
- **搭配**: abstract idea, abstract art, in the abstract
- **例句**:
- Beauty is an abstract concept.
- The paper begins with an abstract.
- **考频**: 44
## absurd

- **音标**: әb'sә:d
- **词性**: adj./n.
- **释义**: ==a. 荒谬的, 不合理的, 可笑的\nn. 荒诞==
- **英文释义**: n. a situation in which life seems irrational and meaningless\ns. inconsistent with reason or logic or common sense\ns. incongruous; inviting ridicule
- **同义词**: ridiculous, preposterous
- **反义词**: reasonable, sensible
- **词根词缀**: ab(偏离)+surd(声音)→声音不协调→荒谬的
- **搭配**: absurd idea, absurd situation, absurdly exaggerated
- **例句**:
- It's absurd to think that the earth is flat in the 21st century.
- The play explores the absurd of modern bureaucracy through dark humor.
- **考频**: 15
## abuse

- **音标**: ә'bju:s.ә'bju:z
- **释义**: ==n. 滥用, 虐待, 恶习, 辱骂\nvt. 滥用, 辱骂, 虐待==
- **英文释义**: n. a rude expression intended to offend or hurt\nv. use foul or abusive language towards\nv. use wrongly or improperly or excessively
- **同义词**: misuse, mistreat
- **反义词**: protect, use
- **词根词缀**: ab(偏离)+use(使用)→不当使用→滥用
- **搭配**: drug abuse, abuse of power, verbal abuse
- **例句**:
- Drug abuse is a serious problem.
- He was accused of abusing his power.
- **考频**: 56
## accent

- **音标**: 'æksәnt
- **词性**: n./vt.
- **释义**: ==n. 重音, 口音, 特点, 注重点\nvt. 重读, 加重音号于, 强调==
- **英文释义**: n. distinctive manner of oral expression\nn. a diacritical mark used to indicate stress or placed above a vowel to indicate a special pronunciation
- **同义词**: stress, intonation, dialectal feature
- **反义词**: neutral pronunciation, standard articulation
- **词根词缀**: ad-(to)+centum(100, via Latin 'cantus' meaning 'song' or 'singing')→ originally 'to sing along with' → evolved to mean 'to mark for prominence in speech' → n. prominent stress or distinctive pronunciation; vt. to emphasize or mark phonetically
- **搭配**: foreign accent, regional accent, place emphasis on (synonymous usage in verb sense)
- **例句**:
- Her French accent made her English sound especially elegant.
- The teacher asked students to accent the second syllable of 'photograph'.
- **考频**: 12
## accident

- **音标**: 'æksidәnt
- **释义**: ==n. 意外事件, 机遇, 事故, 次要方面\n[化] 意外事故; 事故==
- **英文释义**: n. an unfortunate mishap; especially one causing damage or injury\nn. anything that happens suddenly or by chance without an apparent cause
- **同义词**: crash, mishap
- **词根词缀**: ac(加强)+cid(落下)+ent→意外落下→事故
- **例句**:
- He was injured in a car accident.
- It was no accident that they met.
- **考频**: 209
## accommodation

- **音标**: ә.kɒmә'deiʃәn
- **词性**: n.
- **释义**: ==n. 膳宿, 预订铺位, 适应性调节, 调和, 贷款\n[医] 调节(眼); 适应==
- **英文释义**: n. a settlement of differences\nn. in the theories of Jean Piaget: the modification of internal representations in order to accommodate a changing knowledge of reality\nn. living quarters provided for public convenience\nn. the act of providing something (lodging or seat or food) to meet a need
- **同义词**: lodging, housing, adjustment
- **反义词**: inflexibility, rigidity
- **词根词缀**: ac-(to)+commod-(fit, suit)+-ation(noun suffix)→'to fit or suit together'→a process or result of fitting, adapting, or providing suitable living/functional conditions
- **搭配**: make accommodation for, accommodation booking, on-campus accommodation
- **例句**:
- The hotel offers excellent accommodation for international visitors.
- Her eyes' accommodation to low light took several minutes after leaving the bright room.
- **考频**: 36
## accomplish

- **音标**: /əˈkʌmplɪʃ/
- **词性**: v.
- **释义**: ==完成，实现，达到==
- **英文释义**: to succeed in doing or completing something
- **同义词**: achieve, complete, fulfill, attain
- **反义词**: fail, abandon
- **词根词缀**: ac(加强)+compl(完成)+ish→完成
- **搭配**: accomplish a task, accomplish goals, accomplish a mission
- **例句**:
- She accomplished her mission successfully.
- We have accomplished all we set out to do.
- **考频**: 57
## account

- **音标**: ә'kaunt
- **词性**: n./v.
- **释义**: ==n. 报告, 解释, 估价, 理由, 利润, 算账, 帐目\nvi. 报帐, 解释, 导致, 报偿, 占, 杀死\nvt. 认为\n[计] 帐户, 帐号==
- **英文释义**: n. a formal contractual relationship established to provide for regular banking or brokerage or business services\nn. importance or value\nn. a statement of recent transactions and the resulting balance\nn. the quality of taking advantage
- **同义词**: report, description
- **反义词**: ignorance, unawareness
- **词根词缀**: ac(加强)+count(计算)→计算→账户
- **搭配**: account for, take into account, on account of
- **例句**:
- She gave a detailed account of the incident to the police.
- His actions account for the company's recent success.
- **考频**: 328
## accuracy

- **音标**: 'ækjurәsi
- **词性**: n.
- **释义**: ==n. 精确, 正确\n[计] 准确度==
- **英文释义**: n. the quality of being near to the true value\nn. (mathematics) the number of significant figures given in a number
- **同义词**: precision, exactness
- **反义词**: inaccuracy
- **词根词缀**: accur(精确)+acy→准确性
- **搭配**: high accuracy, accuracy rate, improve accuracy
- **例句**:
- The accuracy of the GPS device is within three meters.
- Scientists must ensure the accuracy of their measurements before publishing results.
- **考频**: 33
## accurate

- **音标**: /ˈækjərət/
- **词性**: adj.
- **释义**: ==精确的，准确的==
- **英文释义**: correct, true or exact
- **同义词**: precise, exact, correct
- **反义词**: inaccurate, wrong, imprecise
- **词根词缀**: ac(加强)+cur(关心)+ate→一再关心→精确的
- **搭配**: accurate data, accurate description, accurate measurement
- **例句**:
- The report provides an accurate account of the events.
- Accurate data is essential for research.
- **考频**: 66
## accustom

- **音标**: ә'kʌstәm
- **词性**: v.t.
- **释义**: ==vt. 使习惯于==
- **英文释义**: v make psychologically or physically used (to something)
- **同义词**: habituate, acclimate, familiarize
- **反义词**: alienate, disaccustom
- **词根词缀**: ad-(to, toward)+custom(习惯)→字面义‘向习惯靠近’→通过重复接触使某人逐渐适应某事物→使习惯于
- **搭配**: accustom oneself to sth, accustom sb to sth, accustom to doing sth
- **例句**:
- She had to accustom herself to the cold climate after moving to Canada.
- It takes time to accustom children to a new school routine.
## ache

- **音标**: eik
- **词性**: ['n.', 'vi.']
- **释义**: ==n. 疼痛\nvi. 痛, 哀怜, 渴望==
- **英文释义**: n. a dull persistent (usually moderately intense) pain\nv. have a desire for something or someone who is not present\nv. be the source of pain
- **同义词**: pain, hurt, throb
- **反义词**: relief, numbness
- **词根词缀**: Proto-Germanic *akiz (pain, sorrow) → Old English āce → no productive modern affix; the word is root-only, reflecting an ancient Indo-European root *ag- (to sharpen, be painful) → semantic shift from 'sharp sensation' to generalized physical or emotional pain
- **搭配**: headache, toothache, ache for something
- **例句**:
- My head has been throbbing with a dull ache all morning.
- She ached for her family after moving overseas.
- **考频**: 14
## achieve

- **音标**: ә'tʃi:v
- **释义**: ==vt. 完成, 达到\nvi. 如愿以偿==
- **英文释义**: v. to gain with effort
- **同义词**: accomplish, attain
- **反义词**: fail
- **词根词缀**: ac(加强)+chiev(头)+e→达到头部→实现
- **搭配**: achieve success, achieve a goal
- **例句**:
- She achieved her goal of becoming a doctor.
- Hard work helps you achieve success.
- **考频**: 232
## acid

- **音标**: 'æsid
- **词性**: ['n.', 'adj.']
- **释义**: ==n. 酸, 酸类物质, 尖刻, 迷幻药\na. 酸的, 酸性的, 尖刻的, 敏锐的\n[计] 自动文档互参与索引生成程序==
- **英文释义**: n. any of various water-soluble compounds having a sour taste and capable of turning litmus red and reacting with a base to form a salt\nn. street name for lysergic acid diethylamide\ns. having the characteristics of an acid
- **同义词**: sour substance, corrosive, acrid
- **反义词**: base, alkaline
- **词根词缀**: acid(酸)→酸的
- **搭配**: strong acid, weak acid, acid rain
- **例句**:
- Lemon juice contains citric acid, which gives it a tart flavor.
- Her acid remarks during the meeting left everyone uncomfortable.
- **考频**: 13
## acquaint

- **音标**: ә'kweint
- **词性**: v.t.
- **释义**: ==vt. 使认识, 介绍==
- **英文释义**: v. inform
- **同义词**: familiarize, introduce, inform
- **反义词**: alienate, isolate
- **词根词缀**: ac(加强)+quaint(知道)→使知道→使了解
- **搭配**: acquaint someone with something, acquaint oneself with something, become acquainted with something
- **例句**:
- She acquainted him with the company's policies during orientation.
- The manual acquaints users with basic troubleshooting procedures.
- **考频**: 15
## acquaintance

- **音标**: ә'kweintәns
- **词性**: n.
- **释义**: ==n. 认识, 相识者==
- **英文释义**: n. personal knowledge or information about someone or something\nn. a relationship less intimate than friendship\nn. a person with whom you are acquainted
- **同义词**: associate, acquaint, contact
- **反义词**: stranger, enemy
- **词根词缀**: ac-(to)+quaint(知道)+-ance(名词后缀)→使知道→使人相互知晓→由此引申为‘认识’或‘相识者’
- **搭配**: make one's acquaintance, by acquaintance, a mere acquaintance
- **例句**:
- She’s not a close friend, just an acquaintance from work.
- He made the acquaintance of several scholars at the conference.
- **考频**: 22
## acquire

- **音标**: /əˈkwaɪər/
- **词性**: v.
- **释义**: ==获得，取得；学到==
- **英文释义**: to obtain or gain something; to learn or develop a skill
- **同义词**: obtain, gain, attain, secure
- **反义词**: lose, give up, forfeit
- **词根词缀**: ac(加强)+quire(追求)→获得
- **搭配**: acquire knowledge, acquire skills, acquire experience
- **例句**:
- She acquired a good knowledge of English.
- The company acquired new technology.
- **考频**: 141
## acquisition

- **音标**: .ækwi'ziʃәn
- **词性**: n.
- **释义**: ==n. 获得, 获得物\n[经] 收购, 招揽, 取得==
- **英文释义**: n. the act of contracting or assuming or acquiring possession of something\nn. something acquired
- **同义词**: acquirement, attainment, procurement
- **反义词**: loss, surrender
- **词根词缀**: ac-(to) + quisit-(seek, ask; from Latin 'quaerere') + -ion(noun-forming suffix)→ 'the act of seeking and obtaining' → 'the act or process of acquiring something; something acquired'
- **搭配**: acquisition cost, acquisition strategy, acquisition of skills
- **例句**:
- The company announced the acquisition of a smaller tech startup to expand its AI capabilities.
- Language acquisition in early childhood is typically faster and more intuitive than in adulthood.
- **考频**: 36
## actual

- **音标**: 'æktʃuәl
- **词性**: adj.
- **释义**: ==a. 真实的, 实际的, 现行的\n[医] 实际死亡率==
- **英文释义**: a. presently existing in fact and not merely potential or possible\ns. taking place in reality; not pretended or imitated\ns. being or reflecting the essential or genuine character of something\ns. existing in act or fact
- **同义词**: real, actual, factual, genuine
- **反义词**: hypothetical, theoretical
- **词根词缀**: act(做，行动)+ -ual(形容词后缀，表‘属于…的’或‘与…有关的’)→与‘行动/事实’相关的→真实的，实际发生的
- **搭配**: actual cost, actual figure, actual performance
- **例句**:
- The actual cost of the project was much higher than the initial estimate.
- She didn’t attend the meeting in person, but her actual presence wasn’t required.
- **考频**: 100
## acute

- **词性**: adj.
- **释义**: ==a. 尖锐的, 敏锐的, 激烈的, 严重的, 急性的\n[医] 急性的; 尖锐的==
- **英文释义**: a. having or experiencing a rapid onset and short but severe course\ns. extremely sharp or intense\ns. having or demonstrating ability to recognize or draw fine distinctions\na. of an angle; less than 90 degrees
- **同义词**: severe, sharp
- **反义词**: mild, dull
- **词根词缀**: ac(尖)+ute→尖锐的→敏锐的
- **搭配**: acute pain, acute awareness, acute shortage
- **例句**:
- The patient is suffering from an acute allergic reaction.
- She has an acute sense of hearing and can detect the faintest sounds.
- **考频**: 19
## adore

- **音标**: ә'dɒ:
- **词性**: v.
- **释义**: ==vt. 崇拜, 爱慕, 喜爱\nvi. 崇拜, 爱慕==
- **英文释义**: v. love intensely
- **同义词**: love, worship, cherish
- **反义词**: despise, hate
- **词根词缀**: ad-(to, toward)+ore-(to pray, from Latin 'orare')→'to pray to' or 'direct worship toward'→ intensify into strong emotional devotion or love
- **搭配**: adore someone, adore doing something, absolutely/utterly adore
- **例句**:
- She absolutely adores her new puppy.

## advanced

- **音标**: әd'vɑ:nst
- **词性**: adj.
- **释义**: ==a. 在前的, 高级的, 先进的, 年老的\n[法] 预付的, 预支的, 垫付的==
- **英文释义**: s. farther along in physical or mental development\ns. comparatively late in a course of development\ns. ahead of the times\ns. at a higher level in training or knowledge or skill
- **同义词**: sophisticated, modern
- **反义词**: basic
- **词根词缀**: ad-(to, toward)+vance(=go, move, from Latin 'ire' via 'vadere')+ -ed(participle suffix)→ literally 'moved forward' → extended meaning: progressed beyond the basic level → 'advanced'
- **搭配**: advanced technology, advanced learner, advanced stage
- **例句**:
- She is taking an advanced course in quantum physics.
- The hospital uses advanced imaging technology for early diagnosis.

## air conditioning

- **音标**: /ˈeər kənˈdɪʃənɪŋ/
- **词性**: n.
- **释义**: ==用空调设备调节空气, 空调设备\n[计] 空调; 空气调节==
- **英文释义**: The process of cooling, heating, humidifying, or dehumidifying air to achieve comfortable indoor conditions.
- **同义词**: AC, climate control, air con
- **词根词缀**: air(空气)+conditioning(调节；源自拉丁语conditio '状态，条件'，此处为动名词形式，表'使…处于某种适宜状态')→对空气进行温度、湿度、洁净度等条件调控→空调；空气调节
- **搭配**: air conditioning unit, install air conditioning, air conditioning system
- **例句**:
- Modern office buildings rely heavily on air conditioning to maintain a productive working environment.
- During the heatwave, the lack of air conditioning in the old dormitory made it nearly unbearable to study.
## albeit

- **音标**: ɔ:l'bi:it
- **词性**: conj.
- **释义**: ==conj. 尽管, 虽然==
- **英文释义**: conj. Even though; although; notwithstanding.
- **同义词**: although, though, even though
- **词根词缀**: all(全部)+be(it)+it(古英语宾格代词，表‘此’或‘它’)→字面义‘尽管是全部（如此）’→引申为让步连词‘尽管，虽然’
- **搭配**: albeit + adjective, albeit + adverb, albeit + noun phrase
- **例句**:
- The plan was successful, albeit costly.
- She accepted the offer, albeit with some hesitation.
## album

- **音标**: 'ælbәm
- **词性**: n.
- **释义**: ==n. 粘贴簿, 唱片套\n[医] 白色物==
- **英文释义**: n. one or more recordings issued together; originally released on 12-inch phonograph records (usually with attractive record covers) and later on cassette audiotape and compact disc\nn. a book of blank pages with pockets or envelopes; for organizing photographs or stamp collections etc
- **同义词**: scrapbook, photograph album, record album
- **词根词缀**: albus(拉丁语，意为'白色')+ -um(中性名词后缀)→原指古罗马时期用白蜡涂覆的书写板（tabula alba），后引申为记录文字/图像的簿册→粘贴簿；因早期唱片套内衬常为白色纸板，且作为音乐作品集合载体，故引申为'唱片集'
- **搭配**: photo album, music album, album cover
- **例句**:
- She carefully pasted her vacation photos into a leather-bound album.
- The band's latest studio album debuted at number one on the Billboard chart.
- **考频**: 11
## alcohol

- **音标**: 'ælkәhɒl
- **词性**: n.
- **释义**: ==n. 酒精, 酒\n[化] 醇; 乙醇; 酒精==
- **英文释义**: n. a liquor or brew containing alcohol as the active agent\nn. any of a series of volatile hydroxyl compounds that are made from hydrocarbons by distillation
- **同义词**: ethanol, spirits, booze
- **词根词缀**: Arabic 'al-kuḥl'(fine powder, later distilled essence)+English lexicalization→'al-' (definite article) + 'kuḥl' (originally antimony powder used as eyeliner; later extended to any purified or distilled substance)→via alchemy to denote distilled spirits, then specifically ethanol
- **搭配**: alcohol abuse, alcohol content, alcohol poisoning
- **例句**:
- Excessive alcohol consumption can damage the liver.
- This hand sanitizer contains 70% alcohol by volume.
- **考频**: 97

- **释义**: ==n. 忠贞, 效忠==
- **英文释义**: n. the loyalty that citizens owe to their country (or subjects to their sovereign)
- **同义词**: loyalty, fidelity, devotion
- **反义词**: disloyalty, treason
- **词根词缀**: Latin 'ad-'(to) + 'ligare'(to bind) → 'alligare' (to bind to) → Old French 'allegiance' → bound to a ruler or cause → loyalty and commitment owed to a sovereign, nation, or principle
- **搭配**: swear allegiance, pledge allegiance, allegiance to [a person/cause/country]
- **例句**:
- Citizens swear allegiance to the constitution during the naturalization ceremony.
- Her unwavering allegiance to the cause inspired everyone around her.

- **音标**: /ænˈtɪsɪpeɪt/
- **词性**: v.
- **释义**: ==预期，预料；期望==
- **英文释义**: to expect that something will happen and act accordingly
- **同义词**: expect, foresee, predict, predict
- **反义词**: surprise, miss
- **词根词缀**: anti(前)+cip(拿)+ate→提前拿主意→预期
- **搭配**: anticipate demand, anticipate problems, widely anticipated
- **例句**:
- We anticipate that sales will rise next year.
- No one anticipated the magnitude of the crisis.
- **考频**: 62
## anywhere

- **词根词缀**: any(any)+where(place)→任何地方

- **英文释义**: to express regret or remorse for a fault, mistake, or offense

- **例句**:
- She apologised sincerely for missing the deadline, acknowledging the impact on the team's progress.
- The company issued a formal statement apologising for the data breach and outlined steps to prevent future incidents.
## apology

- **英文释义**: a statement expressing regret for an offense or mistake; a formal defense or justification of a belief or course of action

## bewilder

- **音标**: bi'wildә
- **释义**: vt. 使迷惑, 使不知所措
- **英文释义**: to confuse or puzzle someone so much that they cannot think clearly or decide what to do
- **词根词缀**: be(使)+wilder(荒野)→使迷失荒野→迷惑
- **例句**:
- The sudden change in policy bewildered even the most experienced analysts.
- She was utterly bewildered by the complex legal terminology used in the contract.
- **考频**: 2
## bias

- **音标**: 'baiәs
- **释义**: n. 偏见, 斜纹\na. 偏斜的\nadv. 偏斜\nvt. 使有偏见\n[计] 偏流; 偏压; 偏磁; 偏离
- **英文释义**: a preference or inclination, especially one that inhibits impartial judgment
- **词根词缀**: bias(斜线)→偏见
- **例句**:
- Media coverage often reflects the political bias of its owners.
- Researchers must control for potential bias in experimental design to ensure validity.
- **考频**: 54
## bite

- **音标**: bait
- **释义**: n. 咬, 一口\nv. 咬, 刺痛, 穿透
- **英文释义**: to use teeth to cut into or grip something; a small amount of food taken into the mouth; a sharp, stinging pain or effect
- **词根词缀**: bit(咬)+e→咬
- **例句**:
- The dog gave a sudden bite to the intruder's ankle.
- The bitter economic reforms have begun to bite, causing widespread public discontent.
- **考频**: 22
## bizarre

- **音标**: /bɪˈzɑːr/
- **词性**: adj.
- **释义**: 奇异的，古怪的，异乎寻常的
- **英文释义**: very strange or unusual
- **同义词**: strange, weird, eccentric, peculiar
- **反义词**: normal, ordinary, conventional
- **词根词缀**: 来自意大利语bizzarro（愤怒的）→古怪的
- **搭配**: bizarre behavior, bizarre phenomenon, highly bizarre
- **例句**:
- He has a bizarre sense of humor.
- A bizarre phenomenon occurred.
- **考频**: 10
## blackboard

- **音标**: 'blækbɒ:d
- **释义**: n. 黑板
- **英文释义**: A large, dark, smooth surface, typically made of slate or a similar material, used in classrooms for writing with chalk.
- **词根词缀**: black(黑)+board(板)→黑色的板→黑板
- **例句**:
- The professor wrote the key equations on the blackboard to illustrate the theorem.
- Students were asked to solve the problem step by step on the blackboard in front of the class.
- **考频**: 1
## blame

- **音标**: bleim
- **释义**: n. 过失, 责备\nvt. 责备, 归咎于
- **英文释义**: responsibility for a fault or wrong; to hold someone responsible for something bad
- **词根词缀**: blam(责备)+e→责备
- **例句**:
- The company refused to accept blame for the data breach.
- She blamed the delay on unexpected technical difficulties.
- **考频**: 100
## blast

- **音标**: blæst
- **释义**: n. 一阵风, 爆炸, 枯萎病\nvt. 炸, 使枯萎\nvi. 炸, 猛攻, 猛烈抨击, 枯萎
- **英文释义**: A sudden, violent burst of air, energy, or sound; or the act of exploding or destroying something with explosives.
- **词根词缀**: blast(爆炸)→爆炸
- **例句**:
- The blast from the explosion shattered windows two blocks away.
- Critics blasted the policy as economically unsound and socially irresponsible.
- **考频**: 8
## blaze

- **音标**: bleiz
- **释义**: n. 火焰, 烈火, 光辉\nvi. 燃烧, 发光\nvt. 使燃烧, 宣布, 在树皮上刻痕
- **英文释义**: a bright flame or intense fire; also used figuratively for brilliant light, sudden activity, or strong emotion
- **词根词缀**: blaz(火焰)+e→火焰
- **例句**:
- The forest blaze raged out of control for three days, prompting mass evacuations.
- Her debut novel blazed onto the literary scene, earning critical acclaim and a major award.
- **考频**: 6
## blend

- **音标**: blend
- **释义**: vt. 混合\nn. 混合
- **英文释义**: to mix (substances or qualities) together smoothly so that they become one
- **词根词缀**: blend(混合)→混合
- **例句**:
- The chef carefully blended olive oil, lemon juice, and herbs to create a delicate vinaigrette.
- Her writing style is a sophisticated blend of academic rigor and narrative fluency, making complex ideas accessible to a broad audience.
- **考频**: 8
## blog

- **释义**: n. 博客；部落格；网络日志
- **英文释义**: A regularly updated website or web page, typically run by an individual or small group, written in an informal or conversational style.
- **词根词缀**: web(网络)+log(日志)→网络日志→博客
- **例句**:
- She maintains a blog on sustainable living, which has gained a large academic following.
- The professor recommended several authoritative blogs for students to supplement their research on digital media.
- **考频**: 24
## bloody

- **音标**: 'blʌdi
- **释义**: a. 血腥的, 嗜杀的, 有血的
- **英文释义**: involving or characterized by bloodshed or violence
- **词根词缀**: blood(血)+y(形容词)→血的→血腥的
- **例句**:
- The conflict escalated into a bloody civil war that lasted over a decade.
- Historians describe the battle as one of the bloodiest in medieval European history.
- **考频**: 2
## bloom

- **音标**: blu:m
- **释义**: n. 花, 开花, 青春, 钢块\nvi. 开花, 焕发青春, 茂盛\nvt. 使茂盛, 把...轧成钢坯
- **英文释义**: n. a flower; the state of flowering or flourishing; peak condition of health, beauty, or vitality; vt./vi. to produce flowers or develop in a healthy, vigorous way
- **词根词缀**: bloom(花)→开花
- **例句**:
- The cherry trees are in full bloom along the avenue, attracting countless tourists.
- After years of dedicated study, her intellectual abilities finally began to bloom.
- **考频**: 12
## blossom

- **音标**: 'blɒsәm
- **释义**: n. 花, 花开的状态, 兴旺期\nvi. 开花, 兴旺, 发展
- **英文释义**: a flower or a mass of flowers on a plant; the state or period of flourishing or rapid development
- **词根词缀**: blossom(花)→开花
- **例句**:
- The cherry trees will blossom in early spring, attracting thousands of visitors.
- After years of dedicated practice, her musical talent finally began to blossom.
- **考频**: 2
## blueprint

- **音标**: 'blu:'print
- **释义**: n. 蓝图, 设计图, (周详的)计划\nvt. 制成蓝图, 计划
- **英文释义**: A detailed plan or outline for something, especially one that serves as a basis for action or development
- **词根词缀**: blue(蓝)+print(印刷)→蓝图
- **例句**:
- The government unveiled a comprehensive blueprint for national digital infrastructure by 2030.
- Before launching the startup, the team spent months refining their business blueprint to attract venture capital.
- **考频**: 19
## blunder

- **音标**: 'blʌndә
- **释义**: n. 大错, 大失策\nvi. 失策, 跌跌撞撞地走, 犯错\nvt. 做错
- **英文释义**: a stupid or careless mistake, especially one with serious consequences
- **词根词缀**: blund(笨)+er(人)→笨人→犯错
- **例句**:
- His blunder in misquoting the statute undermined the entire legal argument.
- The minister resigned after a major policy blunder that triggered public outrage.
- **考频**: 6

## board

- **英文释义**: A flat, rigid piece of material (often wood or metal); the deck of a ship; meals provided regularly (e.g., room and board); a group of people who manage an organization; to get on a vehicle, especially a ship or aircraft.
- **词根词缀**: board(板)→板
- **例句**:
- The startup secured funding after presenting its business plan to the board of directors.
- All passengers must board the plane at least 30 minutes before departure.

## bolt

- **音标**: bәult
- **释义**: n. 门闩, 螺钉, 筛子, 闪电, 意外事件\nvt. 闩住, 发射, 脱口而出, 筛, 囫囵吞下\nvi. 囫囵吞枣, 射箭, 脱缰, 退出党派\nadv. 突然
- **英文释义**: A sudden, rapid, or involuntary action; a metal pin or screw used for fastening; a flash of lightning; to move or speak abruptly and forcefully.
- **词根词缀**: bolt(螺栓)→螺栓
- **例句**:
- The candidate bolted from the party after disagreeing with its new policy on climate change.

## boost

- **音标**: /buːst/
- **词性**: v./n.
- **释义**: 促进，增加；提高，鼓励
- **英文释义**: to help or encourage something to increase or improve
- **同义词**: increase, enhance, promote, improve
- **反义词**: decrease, reduce, hinder
- **词根词缀**: 拟声词，来自boost（推）→推动→促进
- **搭配**: boost confidence, boost sales, boost productivity
- **例句**:
- The policy boosted economic growth.
- The victory gave her confidence a boost.
- **考频**: 123

## bore

- **例句**:

## bound

- **音标**: /baʊnd/

- **释义**: 一定的，必定的；跳跃；受约束的
- **英文释义**: certain to happen or to do something; to jump; restricted by a rule
- **同义词**: certain, destined, leap, restricted
- **反义词**: unlikely, free, unrestricted
- **词根词缀**: 来自bind（绑）→受约束的
- **搭配**: bound to, bound by, bound up with
- **例句**:
- She is bound to succeed.
- The dog bounded across the field.
- **考频**: 8

## branch

## brevity

- **音标**: 'breviti
- **释义**: n. 短暂, 简短
- **英文释义**: The quality of being brief in duration or expression
- **词根词缀**: brev(短)+ity(名词)→简短
- **例句**:
- Her speech was admired for its clarity and brevity.
- In academic writing, brevity is valued alongside precision and rigor.
- **考频**: 1
## bridge

- **音标**: bridʒ
- **释义**: n. 桥, 舰桥, 桥梁, 桥牌\nvt. 架桥于, 跨越\n[计] 桥, 网桥, 桥接器
- **英文释义**: A structure built to span a physical obstacle such as a body of water, valley, or road; also used metaphorically for connecting two things or concepts.
- **词根词缀**: bridge(桥)→桥
- **例句**:
- The ancient stone bridge has stood for over eight hundred years.
- Effective communication can bridge the gap between different cultural backgrounds.
- **考频**: 61
## brief

- **音标**: bri:f
- **释义**: n. 摘要, 简报\na. 简短的, 短暂的\nvt. 对...作简报, 摘要, 节录
- **英文释义**: n. a short summary or official statement; a. lasting only a short time or expressed in few words; vt. to give someone essential information quickly
- **词根词缀**: brief(短)→简短的
- **例句**:
- The lawyer submitted a legal brief outlining the key arguments before the hearing.
- Before the meeting, the project manager briefed the team on the latest developments and upcoming deadlines.
- **考频**: 71
## briefcase

- **音标**: 'bri:fkeis
- **释义**: n. 公事包

- **词根词缀**: brief(短)+case(箱子)→装文件的箱子→公文包
- **例句**:
- She placed her laptop and presentation slides into the briefcase before heading to the board meeting.
- The lawyer carried a well-worn briefcase containing confidential client files.
- **考频**: 6

## buffer

- **音标**: 'bʌfә

- **英文释义**: A temporary storage area in memory or a device that holds data while it is being transferred between two processes or devices operating at different speeds.
- **词根词缀**: buff+-er(…的人/…物/更…)
- **例句**:
- The operating system uses a buffer to store incoming data from the keyboard until the CPU is ready to process it.
- To prevent data loss during high-speed transmission, network protocols often employ a buffer to absorb bursts of traffic.

## complaint

- **音标**: kәm'pleint
- **释义**: n. 诉苦, 抱怨, 控诉\n[医] 陈诉; 病
- **英文释义**: A statement expressing dissatisfaction, pain, or a formal accusation.
- **词根词缀**: com(加强)+plain(捶胸)+t(名词)→抱怨
- **例句**:
- The patient's chief complaint was persistent lower back pain.
- Several customers filed a formal complaint about the defective product.
- **考频**: 105
## compress

- **音标**: kәm'pres
- **释义**: vt. 压缩, 压紧\nvi. 受压缩小\n[计] 压缩程序
- **英文释义**: to press or squeeze something into a smaller space or volume
- **词根词缀**: com(一起)+press(压)→压在一起→压缩
- **例句**:
- The software can compress large video files without significant loss of quality.
- When the gas is cooled, it tends to compress and occupy less volume.
- **考频**: 6
## compulsory

- **音标**: kәm'pʌlsәri
- **释义**: a. 被强制的, 强迫的, 义务的\n[经] 强迫的, 强制的
- **英文释义**: required by law or rules; obligatory
- **词根词缀**: com(一起)+puls(推)+ory(形容词)→推到一起的→强制的
- **例句**:
- Attendance at the safety briefing is compulsory for all new employees.
- In most European countries, secondary education is compulsory until the age of 16.
- **考频**: 20
## compute

- **音标**: kәm'pju:t
- **释义**: v. 计算, 估算\nn. 计算, 估算
- **英文释义**: to calculate or determine something, especially using a computer or mathematical methods
- **词根词缀**: com(一起)+put(思考)+e→一起思考→计算
- **例句**:
- The algorithm can compute the shortest path between two nodes in logarithmic time.
- Scientists used supercomputers to compute climate models predicting temperature rise over the next century.
- **考频**: 21
## concrete

- **音标**: 'kɒnkri:t
- **释义**: n. 凝结物, 混凝土\na. 具体的, 实在的, 混凝土的\nv. (使)凝结, 用混凝土浇筑
- **英文释义**: a hard, strong building material made by mixing cement, sand, gravel, and water; also used to describe something specific and tangible rather than abstract
- **词根词缀**: con(一起)+crete(生长)→生长在一起→具体的
- **例句**:
- The architect insisted on using reinforced concrete for the high-rise's structural framework.
- Philosophical debates often shift from abstract theories to concrete examples to clarify meaning.
- **考频**: 34
## concurrent

- **音标**: kәn'kʌrәnt
- **释义**: n. 同时发生的事件\na. 同时发生的, 一致的\n[计] 并行的; 并发的; 同时发生的; 共行的
- **英文释义**: happening or existing at the same time; parallel in time or operation
- **词根词缀**: con(共同/加强)+cur(run/care/cure)+r+-ent(…的/…的人/…剂)→跑/关心
- **例句**:
- The two projects were developed concurrently to maximize resource efficiency.
- Concurrent access to the database by multiple users requires robust locking mechanisms.
## condemn

- **音标**: kәn'dem
- **释义**: vt. 判刑, 责备, 谴责\n[法] 定罪, 判刑, 宣告有罪
- **英文释义**: To express strong disapproval of something or someone, often publicly; to sentence someone to punishment, especially death or imprisonment.
- **词根词缀**: con(加强)+demn(伤害)→强烈伤害→谴责
- **例句**:
- The court condemned the defendant to life imprisonment for the murder.
- Human rights organizations widely condemned the government's crackdown on peaceful protesters.
- **考频**: 13
## condense

- **音标**: kәn'dens
- **释义**: vt. 使浓缩, 使压缩, 缩短\nvi. 浓缩, 凝结
- **英文释义**: to make something denser, shorter, or more concentrated by removing unnecessary parts or by reducing volume
- **词根词缀**: con(一起)+dense(密集)→使密集→压缩
- **例句**:
- The author condensed the 500-page manuscript into a concise 100-page summary.
- When cooled, water vapor condenses into liquid droplets on the surface of the glass.
- **考频**: 7
## conduct

- **音标**: 'kɔndʌkt, -dәkt

- **英文释义**: to organize and carry out an activity; to behave in a particular way; to guide or direct people or processes
- **词根词缀**: con(一起)+duct(引导)→引导一起→指挥
- **例句**:
- The scientist conducted a series of rigorous experiments to test the hypothesis.
- His professional conduct during the negotiation earned him widespread respect.
- **考频**: 173

## consequence

- **英文释义**: a result or effect of an action or condition

## consequently

- **释义**: adv. 所以

- **例句**:
- The company failed to meet regulatory standards; consequently, it was fined heavily.
- She had not prepared for the exam; consequently, her performance was poor.

- **音标**: 'elshwєә
- **释义**: adv. 在别处
- **英文释义**: in or to another place
- **词根词缀**: else(其他)+where(地方)→其他地方
- **例句**:
- If the required materials are not available here, we must look for them elsewhere.
- The committee concluded that the cause of the failure lay elsewhere, not in the software design.
- **考频**: 73

## family

- **音标**: 'fæmәli
- **释义**: n. 家庭, 家人, 族\na. 家庭的
- **英文释义**: a group of people related by blood, marriage, or adoption, typically living together
- **词根词缀**: fam(家庭)+il(形容词)+y(名词)→家庭
- **例句**:
- Her research focuses on the changing structure of the modern family in urban China.
- The court ruled that the child's best interests must take precedence over family tradition.
- **考频**: 1070
## fare

- **音标**: fєә
- **释义**: n. 费用, 旅客, 食物\nvi. 进展, 进步, 经营, 过活
- **英文释义**: n. the price charged for a journey on public transport; a passenger; or food, especially of a particular kind; vi. to perform or get along in a specified way
- **词根词缀**: far(行走)+e→行走的费用→车费
- **例句**:
- The bus fare has increased by 10% this year, adding financial pressure on daily commuters.
- How did the new policy fare in the pilot cities? Early reports suggest it fared well in terms of public acceptance and administrative efficiency.
- **考频**: 33
## farewell

- **音标**: 'fєә'wel
- **释义**: n. 辞别, 再见, 再会\ninterj. 再会
- **英文释义**: a parting expression or ceremony when someone is leaving
- **词根词缀**: fare(行走)+well(好)→一路走好→告别
- **例句**:
- She gave an emotional farewell speech at the graduation ceremony.
- They exchanged warm farewells before he boarded the flight to London.
- **考频**: 4
## fascinate

- **音标**: 'fæsineit
- **释义**: vt. 令人入神, 使着迷\nvi. 入迷
- **英文释义**: to attract and hold someone's attention completely, often by being exciting, mysterious, or beautiful
- **词根词缀**: fascin(魔力)+ate(动词)→使着迷
- **例句**:
- The intricate structure of the human brain continues to fascinate neuroscientists worldwide.
- Her profound insights into classical literature fascinated both professors and graduate students during the seminar.
- **考频**: 5
## favorable

- **音标**: 'feivәrәbl
- **释义**: a. 有利的, 赞许的, 良好的
- **英文释义**: producing good or helpful results; expressing approval or support
- **词根词缀**: favor(喜爱)+able(形容词)→喜爱的→有利的
- **例句**:
- The economic data released last quarter was highly favorable, boosting investor confidence.
- Her research findings received favorable reviews from leading scholars in the field.
- **考频**: 24
## favorite

- **音标**: 'feivәrit
- **释义**: n. 喜欢的事物, 幸运儿\na. 特别受喜爱的, 喜爱的, 宠爱的, 中意的
- **英文释义**: a person or thing that is especially liked or preferred; the most likely to win in a competition
- **词根词缀**: favor(喜爱)+ite(名词/形容词)→最喜爱的
- **例句**:
- Her favorite pastime is reading nineteenth-century British novels.
- Despite being the underdog, the team defeated the tournament favorite in a stunning upset.
- **考频**: 54

- **英文释义**: Having qualities traditionally associated with women, such as delicacy, grace, or gentleness; denoting the female sex or grammatical gender.

## fence

- **音标**: fens
- **释义**: n. 围墙, 栅栏, 买卖赃物的人, 剑术\nvt. 用篱笆围住, 练习剑术, 防护\nvi. 击剑, 搪塞
- **英文释义**: A barrier, typically made of wood or wire, used to enclose an area or separate properties; also, to engage in sword fighting or to evade direct response.
- **词根词缀**: fenc(防御)+e→防御物→篱笆
- **例句**:
- The old farmhouse was surrounded by a weathered wooden fence.
- During the debate, he tried to fence around the controversial question rather than address it directly.
- **考频**: 7
## ferry

- **释义**: n. 渡船, 渡口\n[法] 摆渡营业权, 轮渡
- **英文释义**: A boat or ship used to transport passengers, vehicles, or goods across a body of water.
- **词根词缀**: ferr(运送)+y(名词)→渡船
- **例句**:
- The ferry from Dover to Calais takes about 90 minutes and operates multiple times daily.

## feudal

- **音标**: 'fju:dәl
- **释义**: a. 封建制度的, 封地的, 领地的
- **英文释义**: relating to feudalism, a medieval system in which land was held by lords in exchange for military service and loyalty
- **词根词缀**: feud(封地)+al(形容词)→封建的
- **例句**:
- The feudal hierarchy placed the king at the top, followed by nobles, knights, and peasants.
- Scholars debate whether certain power structures in modern corporations reflect residual feudal dynamics.
- **考频**: 5
## fibre

- **音标**: 'faibә
- **释义**: n. 纤维, 构造, 纤维制品\n[化] 纤维
- **英文释义**: A thin, thread-like structure found in plants, animals, or synthetic materials; also refers to the structural component of food that aids digestion.
- **词根词缀**: fibr(纤维)+e→纤维
- **例句**:
- Dietary fibre is essential for maintaining healthy digestion and preventing constipation.
- The tensile strength of carbon fibre makes it ideal for use in aerospace engineering.
- **考频**: 5

## figure

- **释义**: n. 数字, 价格, 图形, 形状\nvt. 描绘, 表示, 演算, 认为\nvi. 计算, 出现, 估计
- **英文释义**: A numeral, amount, or statistic; a shape or form; to calculate, estimate, or appear prominently.
- **词根词缀**: fig(形状)+ure(名词)→形状→图形,数字
- **例句**:
- The report highlights a sharp rise in unemployment figures, with the latest data showing a 5.2% rate.

- **例句**:

- **英文释义**: at the end of a process or period of time; after a long wait or delay
- **词根词缀**: fin(结束)+al(形容词)+ly(副词)→最终地
- **例句**:
- After years of research, the team finally published their groundbreaking findings in a top-tier journal.
- She struggled with calculus for months but finally mastered the concepts just before the final exam.
- **考频**: 203

- **音标**: heist
- **释义**: n. 匆忙, 急忙
- **英文释义**: great speed or urgency in acting or doing something, often causing carelessness
- **词根词缀**: haste(匆忙)→匆忙
- **例句**:
- He signed the contract in haste and later regretted not reading the fine print.
- The project failed not due to lack of resources, but because of haste in implementation.
- **考频**: 7

## instruct

- **音标**: in'strʌkt
- **释义**: vt. 教, 教育, 命令, 通知\n[法] 托办, 指导, 指示
- **英文释义**: to teach someone how to do something; to order or direct someone formally
- **词根词缀**: in(在)+struct(建造)→建造→指导
- **例句**:
- The professor instructed the students to submit their essays by Friday.
- Before the trial, the judge instructed the jury on the relevant points of law.
- **考频**: 36
## instrumental

- **音标**: .instru'mentәl
- **释义**: a. 仪器的, 器具的, 可作为手段的\n[医] 器械的
- **英文释义**: serving as a means or agent to achieve a result; related to instruments or tools
- **词根词缀**: in(在)+stru(建造)+ment(名词)+al(形容词)→工具的
- **例句**:
- Her leadership was instrumental in the company's successful turnaround.
- The new surgical technique relies on highly precise instrumental procedures.
- **考频**: 6
## insulate

- **音标**: 'insjuleit
- **释义**: vt. 使绝缘, 隔离\n[医] 绝缘
- **英文释义**: to protect something or someone from electricity, heat, cold, or sound by surrounding it with a non-conductive or non-transmitting material
- **词根词缀**: in(在)+sul(岛)+ate(动词)→使成岛→隔离
- **例句**:
- The wires are coated with plastic to insulate them from electrical current.
- Effective policy measures can insulate the domestic economy from external financial shocks.
- **考频**: 6
## insult

- **音标**: 'insʌlt
- **释义**: n. 侮辱, 无礼, 损害\nvt. 损害, 侮辱, 攻击
- **英文释义**: a rude or offensive remark or action that shows disrespect or causes humiliation
- **词根词缀**: in(在)+sult(跳)→跳上去→侮辱
- **例句**:
- His dismissive tone during the debate was widely perceived as a personal insult to the opposing candidate.
- The proposed policy change is not just impractical—it's an insult to decades of scientific consensus on climate change.
- **考频**: 17
## intact

- **音标**: in'tækt
- **释义**: a. 尚未被人碰过的, 原封不动的, 完整的\n[医] 完整的, 无伤的
- **英文释义**: not damaged, altered, or impaired in any way; remaining complete and in original condition
- **词根词缀**: in(不)+tact(接触)→未接触→完整的
- **例句**:
- The ancient manuscript was found intact after centuries buried underground.
- Despite the crash, the black box was recovered intact, providing crucial data for the investigation.
- **考频**: 7
## intend

- **音标**: in'tend
- **释义**: vt. 计划, 打算, 意思是\n[法] 想要, 打算, 意旨
- **英文释义**: to have a plan or purpose to do something
- **词根词缀**: in(向)+tend(伸展)→伸展向→打算
- **例句**:
- The government intends to introduce new legislation on climate change next year.
- She intends to pursue a PhD in linguistics after completing her master's degree.
- **考频**: 156
## intense

- **音标**: in'tens
- **释义**: a. 非常的, 强烈的, 紧张的, 热情的\n[医] 强的
- **英文释义**: having a very strong effect or degree; extreme in intensity
- **词根词缀**: in(加强)+tens(伸展)+e→伸展的→强烈的
- **例句**:
- The athlete felt intense pain after the collision, requiring immediate medical attention.
- She maintained an intense focus on her research, often working late into the night to meet the thesis deadline.

## interest

- **音标**: 'intrist
- **释义**: n. 兴趣, 嗜好, 利息, 利益, 爱好, 趣味, 势力\nvt. 使感兴趣, 与...有关系
- **英文释义**: 1. A feeling of wanting to know or learn about something; 2. Money paid for the use of borrowed money or earned on invested money; 3. A right, share, or stake in something; 4. A person's concern or involvement in a matter.
- **词根词缀**: inter(在…之间)+est(存在)→在中间→兴趣
- **例句**:
- Her deep interest in cognitive linguistics led her to pursue a PhD at Oxford.
- The central bank raised interest rates to curb inflation, affecting both borrowers' loan costs and investors' returns.
- **考频**: 490

## intermittent

- **英文释义**: occurring at irregular intervals; not continuous or steady
- **词根词缀**: inter(在…之间)+mit(送)+t+ent(形容词)→在中间发送→间歇的
- **例句**:
- The patient reported intermittent chest pain, which made diagnosis challenging.

## intersection

- **英文释义**: A point or set where two or more things intersect, such as roads, mathematical sets, or abstract concepts.

- **例句**:

## inverse

- **音标**: in'vә:s
- **释义**: a. 倒转的, 相反的\nn. 反向, 反面\n[计] 反白, 反色
- **英文释义**: Opposite in effect, nature, or order; or a reversed or complementary counterpart.
- **词根词缀**: in(反)+vers(转)+e→反转的
- **例句**:
- The relationship between speed and travel time is inverse: as speed increases, time decreases.
- In linear algebra, multiplying a matrix by its inverse yields the identity matrix.
- **考频**: 2

- **音标**: 'mɒ:tәl
- **释义**: n. 生物, 人类\na. 不免一死的, 人类的, 临终的
- **英文释义**: subject to death; human, especially as contrasted with divine or immortal beings
- **词根词缀**: mort(死)+al(形容词)→必死的→致命的
- **例句**:
- All humans are mortal, and no amount of wealth can exempt one from death.
- The ancient Greeks believed that only mortals suffered from aging and disease, while gods remained eternally youthful.
- **考频**: 3
## mortgage

- **音标**: 'mɒ:gidʒ
- **释义**: n. 抵押, 约束性义务, 抵押借款\nvt. 抵押, 以...作担保, 把...许给
- **英文释义**: A loan secured by real property, typically used to buy a house; also, the legal agreement that gives the lender the right to take the property if the borrower fails to repay.
- **词根词缀**: mort(死)+gage(抵押)→死抵押→抵押
- **例句**:
- After saving for five years, she finally secured a mortgage to purchase her first apartment in London.
- The company mortgaged its headquarters to raise capital for the overseas expansion, a decision that increased its financial risk significantly.
- **考频**: 31

- **英文释义**: A large ensemble of musicians who play various instruments, typically including strings, woodwinds, brass, and percussion, especially for performing classical music.
- **词根词缀**: orchest(舞蹈)+ra(名词后缀)→舞蹈场所→管弦乐队
- **例句**:
- The Vienna Philharmonic Orchestra delivered a breathtaking performance of Beethoven's Seventh Symphony.
- She was accepted into the university's symphony orchestra after passing a rigorous audition.
- **考频**: 10

- **例句**:
- Regular physical exercise is essential for maintaining cardiovascular health and cognitive function.

## resolution

- **音标**: .rezә'lu:ʃәn
- **释义**: n. 解析, 决心, 坚定, 决定, 决议, 消除, 解答, 分解\nn. 图形分辨率\n[计] 图形分辨率
- **英文释义**: A firm decision to do or not to do something; the degree of detail that can be discerned in an image or display; a formal decision made by a group.
- **词根词缀**: re(加强)+solut(解决)+ion(名词)→决心
- **例句**:
- Her resolution to complete the research before the deadline demonstrated remarkable discipline.
- The new monitor supports a maximum resolution of 3840×2160, significantly enhancing visual clarity for data analysis.
- **考频**: 19
## resolve

- **音标**: ri'zɒlv
- **释义**: vi. 决定, 分解, 决心\nvt. 使分解, 解析, 解决, 消除, 决心\nn. 决定之事, 决心, 坚决
- **英文释义**: to make a firm decision to do something; to find a solution to a problem; to separate or break down into constituent parts
- **词根词缀**: re(加强)+solve(解决)→解决
- **例句**:
- After much deliberation, she resolved to pursue a career in public health.
- The committee worked tirelessly to resolve the longstanding dispute between the two departments.
- **考频**: 56
## resort

- **音标**: ri'zɒ:t
- **释义**: n. 度假胜地, 手段, 凭借, 常去之地\nvi. 诉诸, 常去
- **英文释义**: A place frequented for holidays or recreation; or a means or expedient turned to, especially when other options have failed.
- **词根词缀**: re(再次)+sort(出去)→再次出去→度假地
- **例句**:
- The Maldives is a world-famous tropical resort attracting affluent travelers.
- Faced with mounting pressure, the government resorted to emergency legislation to stabilize the economy.
- **考频**: 51
## respective

- **音标**: ri'spektiv
- **释义**: a. 分别的, 各自的
- **英文释义**: belonging or relating to each of the people or things previously mentioned
- **词根词缀**: re(回)+spect(看)+ive(形容词)→回头看→各自的
- **例句**:
- The students returned to their respective classrooms after the assembly.
- The three departments submitted their respective reports by the deadline.
- **考频**: 13
## respond

- **音标**: ri'spɒnd
- **释义**: vt. 以...回答\nvi. 回答, 响应, 回报, 有反应, 承担责任
- **英文释义**: to say or do something as an answer or reaction to something
- **词根词缀**: re(回)+spond(承诺)→回应
- **例句**:
- The government failed to respond promptly to the public's concerns about environmental pollution.
- Patients with this condition often respond well to immunotherapy.
- **考频**: 129
## response

- **音标**: ri'spɒns
- **释义**: n. 反应, 回答, 响应\n[计] 应答
- **英文释义**: a reaction to a stimulus, a reply to a question or communication, or a system's output in computing
- **词根词缀**: re(回)+spons(承诺)+e→回应
- **例句**:
- The government's response to the economic crisis was widely criticized by economists.
- In distributed systems, minimizing network latency is crucial for improving server response time.
- **考频**: 245
## responsibility

## restless

- **音标**: 'restlis
- **释义**: a. 不安静的, 慌张的, 休息不充分的\n[医] 不安静的, 不宁的
- **英文释义**: Unable to rest or relax; feeling anxious, uneasy, or physically uncomfortable.
- **词根词缀**: rest(休息)+less(无)→不安的
- **例句**:
- Her restless energy made it impossible for her to sit through the entire lecture.
- Patients with restless legs syndrome often experience an irresistible urge to move their legs, especially at night.
- **考频**: 4
## resultant

- **音标**: ri'zʌltәnt
- **释义**: a. 结果的, 合成的\nn. 结果, 合力, 生成物
- **英文释义**: occurring or arising as a result; the single vector, force, or quantity that is the sum of two or more component vectors, forces, or quantities
- **词根词缀**: re(再/回/相反)+sult+-ant(…的人/…的)
- **例句**:
- The resultant economic downturn forced many small businesses to close.
- In physics, the resultant of two forces acting at a point can be found using vector addition.
## resume

- **释义**: vt. 重新开始, 取回, 恢复\nvi. 再开始\nn. 摘要, 个人简历\n[计] 继续执行
- **英文释义**: to begin again after an interruption; to summarize; a concise document presenting one's education, work experience, and skills
- **词根词缀**: re(再次)+sume(拿)→重新拿起→恢复
- **例句**:

- **考频**: 68
## retort

- **英文释义**: A quick, clever reply to a criticism or comment; also, a piece of laboratory glassware used for distillation.
- **词根词缀**: re(回)+tort(扭曲)→扭回→反驳
- **例句**:
- Her sharp retort silenced the critic instantly.
- The chemist carefully heated the solution in the retort to separate its components.

## royalty

- **音标**: 'rɒiәlti
- **释义**: n. 皇室, 王族成员, 王权, 特权阶层, 庄严\n[经] 特许权, 使用费, 使用税
- **英文释义**: 1. the king, queen, and other members of a royal family; 2. payment made to a creator or owner for the use of their work, invention, or natural resource
- **词根词缀**: royal(国王的)+ty(名词后缀)→王权
- **例句**:
- The British royalty attracts global attention during state ceremonies and charitable initiatives.
- Software companies often pay royalties to patent holders for using proprietary algorithms.
- **考频**: 2
## rule

- **音标**: ru:l
- **释义**: n. 规则, 统治, 控制, 支配, 规律, 标准, 章程, 破折号, 铅线\nvt. 规定, 统治, 管理, 控制, 支配, 裁决\nvi. 统治, 管辖, 裁定\n[计] 规则, 水线
- **英文释义**: A principle or regulation that governs behavior, procedure, or operation; to exercise authority or control over something or someone.
- **词根词缀**: rul(统治)+e→规则
- **例句**:
- The university has strict rules regarding academic integrity, and violations may result in expulsion.
- The Supreme Court ruled that the law was unconstitutional, thereby setting a binding precedent for future cases.
- **考频**: 397
## rumor

- **音标**: 'ru:mә
- **释义**: n. 谣言, 传闻\nvt. 谣传
- **英文释义**: unverified information or gossip that is spread from person to person
- **词根词缀**: rum(谣言)+or(名词后缀)→谣言
- **例句**:
- The rumor about the CEO's resignation turned out to be completely false.
- It is unwise to act on a rumor without checking its credibility, especially in academic or professional settings.
- **考频**: 8
## rust

- **音标**: rʌst
- **释义**: n. 锈, 生锈, 衰退\nvi. 生锈, 衰退\nvt. 使生锈, 腐蚀
- **英文释义**: a reddish-brown flaky coating formed on iron or steel by oxidation, or the process of its formation; also used figuratively to mean decline or deterioration
- **词根词缀**: rust(锈)→锈
- **例句**:
- The old bicycle had been left outside for years and was completely covered in rust.
- After retiring from competitive sports, she feared her skills would rust without regular practice.
- **考频**: 6
## sack

- **音标**: sæk
- **释义**: n. 麻布袋, 洗劫\nvt. 把...装入袋, 洗劫
- **英文释义**: A coarse bag, typically made of burlap or similar material; also, to plunder or loot a place.
- **词根词缀**: sack(袋)→袋
- **例句**:
- The farmer stored the potatoes in a large burlap sack.
- Historians note that the city was sacked by invading forces in 1453, resulting in widespread destruction and loss of cultural artifacts.
- **考频**: 8
## saddle

- **音标**: 'sædl
- **释义**: n. 鞍, 马鞍, 车座, 鞍状物\nvt. 装以马鞍, 使负担\nvi. 跨上马鞍
- **英文释义**: A seat for a rider, typically on a horse or bicycle; also, to place a burden or responsibility on someone.
- **词根词缀**: sadd(坐)+le(名词后缀)→鞍
- **例句**:
- The rider adjusted the saddle before mounting the horse.
- Young professionals are often saddled with student debt and rising housing costs.
- **考频**: 3
## sake

- **音标**: seik
- **释义**: n. 目的, 缘故, 理由
- **英文释义**: for the purpose or benefit of someone or something
- **词根词缀**: sake(缘故)→缘故
- **例句**:
- She resigned from her job for the sake of her mental health.
- The government imposed strict regulations for the sake of public safety.
- **考频**: 36
## salient

- **音标**: 'seiliәnt
- **释义**: a. 显著的, 突出的, 跳跃的\nn. 凸角, 突出部分
- **英文释义**: prominent, noticeable, or important; jutting out physically
- **词根词缀**: sal(跳)+ient(形容词后缀)→突出的
- **例句**:
- The salient feature of the new policy is its emphasis on sustainability.
- In the battlefield diagram, the enemy held a strategic salient that extended deep into our territory.
- **考频**: 1
## sample

- **音标**: 'sæmpl
- **释义**: n. 样品, 范例, 样本\nvt. 抽样, 尝试\n[计] 示例, 字样
- **英文释义**: A small part or quantity intended to show what the whole is like; to test or examine a part to infer information about the whole.
- **词根词缀**: s(从)+ample(拿)→样品
- **例句**:
- The pharmaceutical company sent us a sample of the new drug for clinical evaluation.
- Before launching the full survey, researchers conducted a pilot study using a random sample of 200 participants.
- **考频**: 118
## sanction

- **音标**: 'sæŋkʃәn
- **释义**: n. 核准, 制裁, 处罚, 约束力\nvt. 制定制裁规则, 认可, 核准, 同意
- **英文释义**: Official permission or approval for an action; or a penalty imposed to enforce compliance with a law or rule.
- **词根词缀**: sanct(神圣)+ion(名词后缀)→批准
- **例句**:
- The government imposed economic sanctions on the country in response to its human rights violations.
- The new policy was sanctioned by the university's board of trustees after months of deliberation.
- **考频**: 14
## sarcastic

- **音标**: sɑ:'kæstik
- **释义**: a. 讽刺的, 讥讽的
- **英文释义**: Using irony to mock or convey contempt
- **词根词缀**: sarc(肉)+astic(形容词后缀)→讽刺的
- **例句**:
- Her sarcastic remark about his 'impressive' punctuality—arriving 45 minutes late—left the room uncomfortably silent.
- The author's sarcastic tone in the essay subtly undermines the argument without stating disagreement outright.
- **考频**: 8
## satire

- **音标**: 'sætaiә
- **释义**: n. 讽刺文学, 讽刺
- **英文释义**: A literary work that uses humor, irony, or exaggeration to criticize and expose human folly or vice.
- **词根词缀**: satir(讽刺)+e→讽刺
- **例句**:
- Jonathan Swift's 'A Modest Proposal' is a classic example of satire targeting British colonial policies.
- The film uses sharp satire to critique social media addiction and performative activism.
- **考频**: 5
## satisfactory

- **音标**: .sætis'fæktәri
- **释义**: a. 满意的, 赎罪的\n[法] 令人满意的, 令当事人满意的, 充分的
- **英文释义**: adequate or acceptable, though not outstanding
- **词根词缀**: satis(足够)+fact(做)+ory(形容词后缀)→令人满意的
- **例句**:
- The candidate's performance in the interview was satisfactory, but not exceptional.
- Although the experimental results were only marginally significant, the researchers deemed them satisfactory for preliminary publication.
- **考频**: 31
## saturate

- **音标**: 'sætʃәreit
- **释义**: vt. 使渗透, 浸透, 使充满, 使饱和\na. 浸透的, 饱和度高的, 深颜色的\nn. 饱和化合物, 饱和脂肪酸
- **英文释义**: to fill something completely with a substance so that no more can be absorbed or dissolved
- **词根词缀**: satur(满)+ate(动词后缀)→使饱和
- **例句**:
- The market is saturated with low-cost smartphones, making it difficult for new brands to gain traction.
- Heavy rainfall saturated the soil, leading to widespread flooding in the region.
- **考频**: 11

## serial

- **音标**: 'siәriәl
- **释义**: n. 分期连载作品, 连载小说\na. 连续的, 一连串的, 连载的, 分期偿还的\n[计] 连续的; 串行的
- **英文释义**: n. a story or program published or broadcast in parts over a period of time; a. occurring in a series, one after another, or issued in installments

- **例句**:
- The novel was first published as a serial in a monthly magazine.

## series

## setting

- **音标**: 'setiŋ
- **释义**: n. 环境, 背景, 布景, 镶嵌, 调整, 沉落, 一副餐具\n[计] 设置

- **英文释义**: A geometric shape with four equal sides and four right angles; also refers to a public open area in a city, a city block, the product of a number multiplied by itself, or an instrument for drawing right angles; as an adjective, it means shaped like a square, honest and fair, or exactly aligned.
- **词根词缀**: square→正方形,广场
- **例句**:
- The architect emphasized symmetry by placing a fountain at the center of the square.
- Her argument does not square with the empirical evidence presented in the study.

- **词根词缀**: suck(吸)→吸
- **例句**:
- The baby began to suck vigorously on the bottle.
- The sponge quickly sucked up the spilled water.
- **考频**: 10

## wash

- **音标**: wɒʃ
- **释义**: n. 洗, 洗涤, 冲洗, 洗的衣服, 冲积物, 洼地\nvt. 洗, 洗涤, 洗清, 用水冲洗, 流过, 弄湿, 粉刷, 镀金属薄层于\nvi. 洗涤, 洗澡, 被冲蚀, 漂浮
- **英文释义**: to clean something with water and often soap; also used as a noun to refer to the act of washing, the clothes being washed, or material deposited by water
- **词根词缀**: wash(洗)→洗
- **例句**:
- She put the delicate blouse in a gentle wash cycle to avoid damage.
- The heavy rain caused the river to overflow, and the wash carried sediment across the farmland.
- **考频**: 32
## waste

- **音标**: weist
- **释义**: n. 浪费, 废物, 损耗, 消耗, 荒地, 垃圾, 地面风化物\na. 废弃的, 荒芜的, 多余的\nvt. 浪费, 消耗, 使荒芜\nvi. 浪费, 消耗, 变消瘦
- **英文释义**: n. the act of using something carelessly or inefficiently; useless or discarded material; land that is barren or uncultivated; v. to use or expend carelessly, to diminish gradually, or to make barren
- **词根词缀**: waste(浪费)→浪费
- **例句**:
- The company implemented new policies to reduce energy waste and improve sustainability.
- Years of neglect have caused the once-fertile farmland to waste away into barren scrubland.
- **考频**: 182
## waterproof

- **音标**: 'wɒtәpru:f
- **释义**: n. 防水材料\na. 不透水的, 防水的\nvt. 使防水
- **英文释义**: impermeable to water; resistant to penetration by water
- **词根词缀**: water(水)+proof(防)→防水的
- **例句**:
- The hiking jacket is made of lightweight, breathable, and fully waterproof fabric.
- Engineers reinforced the basement walls with a waterproof membrane to prevent moisture infiltration.
- **考频**: 3
## weary

- **音标**: 'wiәri
- **释义**: a. 疲倦的, 萎靡的, 厌倦的, 厌烦的\nvt. 使疲倦, 使厌烦\nvi. 疲乏, 生厌, 不耐烦
- **英文释义**: feeling or showing extreme tiredness, lack of energy, or loss of interest
- **词根词缀**: weary(疲倦)→疲倦的
- **例句**:
- After ten hours of intense revision, she felt utterly weary and struggled to focus on the final practice test.
- He grew weary of the repetitive arguments and decided to withdraw from the debate altogether.
- **考频**: 5

- **释义**: n. 欢迎, 欢迎词\na. 受欢迎的, 可随意的, 可喜的\nvt. 欢迎, 接待\ninterj. 欢迎
- **英文释义**: a polite greeting or expression of pleasure at someone's arrival or presence; also used to indicate that something is gladly accepted or encouraged
- **词根词缀**: wel(好)+come(来)→欢迎

## well

- **音标**: wel
- **释义**: n. 井, 泉水, 源泉, 好\nv. 涌出\na. 健康的, 良好的, 适宜的, 恰当的\nadv. 很好地, 适当地, 好意地, 很, 完全\ninterj. 好啦
- **英文释义**: A deep hole dug or drilled to access underground water; also used as an adverb meaning 'in a good, proper, or thorough manner', an adjective meaning 'in good health or condition', a verb meaning 'to flow or rise up (often of liquid)', and an interjection expressing assent or transition.
- **词根词缀**: well(好)→好
- **例句**:
- The village draws its drinking water from a hand-dug well.
- She spoke so well in the debate that she was unanimously selected as the team's representative.
- **考频**: 4065

## whatsoever

- **音标**: .hwɒtsәu'evә
- **释义**: pron. 无论什么
- **英文释义**: at all; in any way or to any degree (used for emphasis, especially after a negative or interrogative word)
- **词根词缀**: what(什么)+so(如此)+ever(任何)→无论什么
- **例句**:
- He has no authority whatsoever to make such decisions.
- I have no intention whatsoever of attending the meeting.
- **考频**: 5
## whereas

- **音标**: hwєәr'æz
- **释义**: conj. 然而, 鉴于\n[法] 考虑到, 鉴于, 就...而论
- **英文释义**: used to introduce a statement that contrasts with or seems to contradict something that has been said previously
- **词根词缀**: where(哪里)+as(作为)→鉴于
- **例句**:
- The government advocates fiscal austerity, whereas many economists argue for increased public spending to stimulate growth.
- Whereas traditional textbooks emphasize rote memorization, modern pedagogical approaches prioritize critical thinking and application.
- **考频**: 62
## whereby

- **音标**: (h)weә'bai
- **释义**: adv. 靠什么, 如何, 为何, 靠那个, 因此, 由此\n[法] 因此, 由是
- **英文释义**: by which; through which; as a result of which
- **词根词缀**: where(哪里)+by(通过)→通过…
- **例句**:
- The agreement includes a clause whereby each party agrees to submit disputes to arbitration.
- The new policy introduces a mechanism whereby employees can report misconduct anonymously.
- **考频**: 12

## zoom

- **音标**: zu:m
- **释义**: n. 急速上升, 变焦摄影, 嗡嗡声\nvi. 猛增, 急速上升, 摄象机移动\nvt. 使摄象机移动\n[计] 缩放
- **英文释义**: to move or increase very quickly; to adjust a camera lens to magnify or reduce the image size
- **词根词缀**: zo(animal)+om
- **例句**:
- The company's profits zoomed by 40% after the successful product launch.
- The documentary used smooth zoom techniques to emphasize the emotional intensity of the scene.
